    </i>

      <p>
       <i>
        <b>
         The Economist
        </b>
       </i>
       is an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English-language" title="English-language">
        English-language
       </a>
       weekly magazine-format
       <a href="/wiki/Newspaper" title="Newspaper">
        newspaper
       </a>
       owned by the
       <a href="/wiki/Economist_Group" title="Economist Group">
        Economist Group
       </a>
       and edited at offices in
       <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">
        London
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about-us_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-about-us-3">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Map_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Map-9">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Continuous publication began under its founder,
       <a href="/wiki/James_Wilson_(businessman)" title="James Wilson (businessman)">
        James Wilson
       </a>
       , in September 1843. In 2015 its average weekly
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magazine_circulation" title="Magazine circulation">
        circulation
       </a>
       was a little over 1.5 million, about half of which were sold in the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pgazette_6-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-pgazette-6">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about-us_3-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-about-us-3">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The publication belongs to the
       <a href="/wiki/Economist_Group" title="Economist Group">
        Economist Group
       </a>
       . It is 50% owned by the
       <a href="/wiki/Rothschild_banking_family_of_England" title="Rothschild banking family of England">
        English branch
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Rothschild_family" title="Rothschild family">
        Rothschild family
       </a>
       and by the
       <a href="/wiki/Agnelli_family" title="Agnelli family">
        Agnelli family
       </a>
       through its holding company
       <a href="/wiki/Exor_(company)" title="Exor (company)">
        Exor
       </a>
       . The remaining 50% is held by private investors including the editors and staff.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Rothschilds and the Agnellis are represented on the board of directors.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A
       <a href="/wiki/Trustee" title="Trustee">
        board of trustees
       </a>
       formally appoints the editor, who cannot be removed without its permission. Although
       <i>
        The Economist
       </i>
       has a global emphasis and scope, about two-thirds of the 75 staff journalists are based in the London borough of
       <a href="/wiki/City_of_Westminster" title="City of Westminster">
        Westminster
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For the year to March 2016 the Economist Group declared operating profit of £61m.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Previous major shareholders include
       <a href="/wiki/Pearson_PLC" title="Pearson PLC">
        Pearson PLC
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <i>
        The Economist
       </i>
       takes
       <a href="/wiki/The_Economist_editorial_stance" title="The Economist editorial stance">
        an editorial stance
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Classical_liberalism" title="Classical liberalism">
        classical
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Economic_liberalism" title="Economic liberalism">
        economic liberalism
       </a>
       that supports
       <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">
        free trade
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Globalisation" title="Globalisation">
        globalisation
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_immigration" title="Free immigration">
        free immigration
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Cultural_liberalism" title="Cultural liberalism">
        cultural liberalism
       </a>
       (such as supporting legal recognition for
       <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">
        same-sex marriage
       </a>
       or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drug_liberalisation" title="Drug liberalisation">
        drug liberalisation
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about-us_3-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-about-us-3">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The publication has described itself as "...a product of the Caledonian
       <a href="/wiki/Classical_liberalism" title="Classical liberalism">
        liberalism
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Adam_Smith" title="Adam Smith">
        Adam Smith
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/David_Hume" title="David Hume">
        David Hume
       </a>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It targets highly educated, cultured readers and claims an audience containing many influential executives and policy-makers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The publication's CEO described this recent global change, which was first noticed in the 1990s and accelerated in the beginning of the 21st century, as a "new age of Mass Intelligence".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

         </a>
         <ul>
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10">
